  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_97b37980-3a7a-4417-8604-05a8dbee5132'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7214948446283816571" style="display:none">The Bonehunters march for Kolanse, led by Adjunct Tavore. This woman with no gifts of magic, deemed plain, unprepossessing, displaying nothing to instill loyalty or confidence, will challenge the gods - if her own mutinous troops don't kill her first.<br /><br />Her enemy, the Forkrul Assail, seek to cleanse the world, to annihilate everything. In the realm of Kurald Galain, home to the long lost city of Kharkanas, a refugees commanded by Yedan Derryg, the Watch, await the breaching of Lightfall, and the coming of the Tiste Liosan. In this war they cannot win, they will die in the name of an empty city and a queen with no subjects. <br /><br />Elsewhere, the three Elder Gods, Kilmandaros, Errastas and Sechul Lath, work to shatter the chains binding Korabas, the Otataral Dragon. Against her force of utter devastation, no mortal can stand. At the Gates of Starvald Demelain, the Azath House sealing the portal is dying. Soon will come the Eleint, dragons, and a final cataclysm.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=masterpieces">masterpieces</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830298715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10464450131267058470"><b>Epic, masterful, and scintillating in every sense of these words; <i>The Crippled God</i> is an unforgettable magnum opus that concludes Steven Erikson’s genre-defining series: <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen.</i></b><br/><br/>11,216 pages (Bantam paperback edition) and 3.3 million words read in exactly two months and two weeks; I’m done, it’s finally over. The entire ten-volume of <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> has been in my TBR pile for almost two years long, and now it has been read, dusted and shelved. Erikson has raised th</span>
  <span id="freeText10464450131267058470" style="display:none"><b>Epic, masterful, and scintillating in every sense of these words; <i>The Crippled God</i> is an unforgettable magnum opus that concludes Steven Erikson’s genre-defining series: <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen.</i></b><br><br>11,216 pages (Bantam paperback edition) and 3.3 million words read in exactly two months and two weeks; I’m done, it’s finally over. The entire ten-volume of <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> has been in my TBR pile for almost two years long, and now it has been read, dusted and shelved. Erikson has raised the benchmark for Epic/military fantasy ridiculously high with what he created in this series. Together with <i>Wrath</i> by John Gwynne and <i>Assassin’s Fate</i> by Robin Hobb, <i>The Crippled God</i> stands among the top of the best final book of a series I’ve ever read, and there’s a definite probability that it will always stay on that list.<br> <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"I have enjoyed our long conversation. What's three and a half million words between friends?" – Steven Erikson</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br> <br>Where do I even begin? Is it even possible for anyone to write a review that can give the series the justice it deserves? I know I can’t. Alas, a review must be written; I’ll try to keep it as short as possible. Having slept on it and waking up thinking about it, I’ve come to realize that I probably will never encounter another fantasy series as complex and massive in scope like this series. Erikson’s achievement in writing <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> and completing the massive series in the span of twelve years deserves a standing ovation from the entire SFF community. Accompanying demonic ambition, writing speed, dedication, and hard work, Erikson has created a series brimming with stellar content that can last a lifetime; I can already envision that rereading the series will be immensely rewarding. <br> <br><i>The Crippled God</i> is the tenth and the final book in the highly acclaimed <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> series and if you’re reading this review, you probably already know that the finale of the series itself was divided into two books, <i>Dust of Dreams</i> and <i>The Crippled God</i>. I personally think that it was unnecessary to divide the finale into two books. Erikson put everything I disliked about the series into <i>Dust of Dreams</i> and everything I loved about the series into <i>The Crippled God</i>. The result? <i>Dust of Dreams</i> became my least favorite book of the series and <i>The Crippled God</i> became one of my absolute favorite books of the series; I loved it as much as I loved <i>Memories of Ice</i> and The Bonehunters. Erikson has successfully delivered an extremely rewarding experience to readers who managed to commit and complete reading the series.<br> <br>Excluding the close to pointless Snake plotline, I thoroughly enjoyed reading every single page of this book. The build-up, the characters’ development, the world-building, and the themes that ran throughout the entire series came to an explosive denouement. The refrains of sacrifice, an orchestra of bittersweet poignancy, impactful themes of faith, despair, redemption, regret, compassion, loyalty, honor, resilience, and friendship; all of these collaborate to give the unwitnessed heroic deeds the proper respect they rightfully deserved.<br> <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“It is not enough to wish for a better world for the children. It is not enough to shield them with ease and comfort. …if we do not sacrifice our own ease, our own comfort, to make the future's world a better one, then we curse our own children. We leave them a misery they do not deserve; we leave them a host of lessons unearned.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br> <br>There were a myriad thought-provoking, inspiring, and resonating philosophical discussions implemented into the story line; combined with the stunningly written act of devastations brought in this last installment, suffice to say that I was repeatedly astonished by Erikson’s tremendous capability as an author. The last two chapters (which lasted approximately 300 pages and took me four hours to read) of <i>The Crippled God</i> were extremely well-written, keeping me on the edge of my seat, and pretty much summed up the best kind of experience that epic fantasy has to offer. Blistering battles for dominance, swirling grief, brutal annihilation, and inescapable casualties from all factions; firestorm, thunderstorm, maelstrom, and many more large-scale action sequences create an exhilarating and emotional cinematic experience. Plus, the accumulation of the tension, build-up, and information that has been established, either explicitly or subtly, throughout the series right from the first installment culminated to bring the most groundbreaking convergence of epic proportions into the last two chapters; it was easily the best climactic sequences of the series and that’s saying a lot.<br> <br>To choose one or five favorite characters from the series is as difficult as being asked to choose which favorite series you’ll burn. Usually, there are less than ten memorable characters within a single trilogy. For example, if I ask who your favorite characters from <i>Mistborn</i> trilogy are, the answers are almost guaranteed to be Kelsier, Kelsier, Kelsier, Kelsier, Kelsier, and Vin; this won’t happen with this series. There are an incredibly high amount of memorable and pivotal characters that being asked to choose only five favorite characters will be such an unfair task. Characterizations have always been the most important aspect in every single book I read. The series has the biggest cast of characters I’ve ever read by far. I’m not joking, there were more than 300 characters throughout the series to keep track of, the dramatis personae in this final installment alone have 212 characters in it. I won’t lie, the characterizations in the second half of the series suffer a lot in my opinion. Erikson introduced new characters mercilessly and the majority of them sounded the same to me. This was especially true in <i>Reaper’s Gale</i> and <i>Dust of Dreams</i>. Fortunately, Erikson didn’t do this in <i>The Crippled God</i>. Only a few new characters were introduced and they were all fantastic to read. By focusing the storytelling and narrative on characters we’re familiar with, regardless of their quantity, made the characters dynamics, interactions, and dialogues an absolute delight to read.<br> <br>I don’t have anything left to say regarding the installment, or the series itself except that Erikson’s world-building was unparalleled. In this blazing colossal conclusion, Erikson unleashed all the races throughout the series. The humans, the gods, the ascendants, K’Chain Chemalle, Forkrul Assail, T’lan Imass, Barghast, Tiste Andii, Tiste Liosan, Tiste Edur, Eleint, practically every kind of factions converged. I have never read a series as massive as this one. Every place, buildings, weapons, characters, and locations - all have their own history. Erikson could seriously write about anything in this world and it would still work. That’s how massive and intricate this series is. Right now, the only thing that in my opinion can be compared to Erikson’s world-building skill is Sanderson’s Cosmere universe, but that’s totally different as Sanderson’s Cosmere spans across worlds and many series instead of taking place in a single world as Malazan did.<br> <br>My advice if you’re new to the series: patience and commitment. Look, there’s no way around it, it doesn’t matter how much you love the series, I guarantee you that these two are necessary. This is especially true in the second half of the series where the scope of the story grew more complex, massive, and difficult than the first half. From my experience, I simply can’t take a break from the series too long otherwise I risk forgetting even more details than I already did; many readers said I finished this series very quickly, I took a one week break twice and even then, I forgot some details already. It’s also impossible to gauge whether you’ll like the series or not just from the first book. My recommendation is this. Give the series a go until <i>Memories of Ice</i>. If upon finishing <i>Memories of Ice</i> you feel the series was just okay, or not suitable to your reading preference, continuing the series from there on will most likely be futile. <i>Memories of Ice</i> is considered by a lot of the fans to be one of the, if not the best installment of the series. However, if you find that you’re blown away already by <i>Gardens of the Moon</i>, you’ll probably experience an escapism fantasy unlike any other.<br><br><b>Picture: <i>The Complete Malazan Book of the Fallen</i>. Cover art by Kekai Kotaki.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539436131i/26443995._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>I didn’t find <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> as flawless—to be fair, no series is ever totally perfect—as what the rabid fans claimed to be. However, despite some issues I had with it, <b>I rank the series as a whole to be my current number one favorite series of all time together with <i>The Faithful and the Fallen</i> by John Gwynne and <i>The Stormlight Archive</i> by Brandon Sanderson</b>. Don’t make me choose which one I love more, they’re different from each other, and each of them has their own strengths. Brilliantly complex and extremely rewarding in all its might, <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> is a transcending and triumphant genre-defining series, and if you’re an epic fantasy fans, you owe it to yourself to give the series a try. I, as a reader, am genuinely gratified to have read the everlasting adventures penned in <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i>. The series and many other incredible series have cemented the fact that epic fantasy, or just fantasy in general, will always be my favorite genre and escapism read.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“And now the page before us blurs.<br>An age is done. The book must close.<br>We are abandoned to history.<br>Raise high one more time the tattered standard<br>Of the Fallen. See through the drifting smoke<br>To the dark stains upon the fabric.<br>This is the blood of our lives, this is the<br>Payment of our deeds, all soon to be<br>Forgotten.<br>We were never what people could be.<br>We were only what we were.<br><br>Remember us.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Joining many other witnessed and unwitnessed readers, I have unchained the Book of Fallen. It’s your turn to carve the tales of the Fallen to your memory and remember them. <br><br><b>
  <u>Series review:</u>

</b><br> <br><b>Side note:</b><br><i>Special thanks to my friends, TS and Emma, who listened to my all my theories and ramblings (for better or worse) about the series without giving spoilers or being judgmental. Lastly, I know some of you have asked about the proposal I mentioned in my <i>Gardens of the Moon</i> review. The answer is yes! It won’t be soon, I still have some things to prepare but fingers crossed it will happen next year. For now, let’s just say that the stoppage light has turned green by completing this series. Wish us the best of luck! :)</i><br><br><b>You can order the book <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780765348876/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE!</a></u></b><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/10/13/the-crippled-god-malazan-book-of-the-fallen-10/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>

<div id="review_1712718608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712718608" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712718608?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765316561" href="/book/show/8706730-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=grim-dark">grim-dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712718608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13152057876658988402"><b>Full review now up!</b><br/><br/>I can’t believe I finally finished this series. Ten books, seven months, thousands of pages, and countless characters later here I am. Wondering how long it will take me before I re-read this series. I know I just finished it, but after spending so many months reading it I find myself out of my routine. I want to march the Chain of Dogs with Coltaine again, I want to fight the Pannion Domin with the Bridgeburners at Coral, and witness the Bonehunters at Y’Ghatan and Malaz City</span>
  <span id="freeText13152057876658988402" style="display:none"><b>Full review now up!</b><br /><br />I can’t believe I finally finished this series. Ten books, seven months, thousands of pages, and countless characters later here I am. Wondering how long it will take me before I re-read this series. I know I just finished it, but after spending so many months reading it I find myself out of my routine. I want to march the Chain of Dogs with Coltaine again, I want to fight the Pannion Domin with the Bridgeburners at Coral, and witness the Bonehunters at Y’Ghatan and Malaz City. Oh so many books on my TBR list and I just want to start this series over. Alas, it is time to move on…..for now.<br /><br />Someone told me the end of this series was satisfying, but kept you wanting more. I have to say I strongly agree with that statement. Most of the storylines were wrapped up nicely, but I am left wondering about a few. No worries! I will not divulge my curiousness in this review, so you need not worry about spoilers going forward.<br /> <br />There are so many amazing things about this series. It is really hard to pick out what I loved most about it. Definitely some of the best and most memorable characters I have ever read about. A world so vast it boggles the mind that anyone could come up with such a detailed piece of art. Or maybe the raw emotion the story brings out in the reader. I can’t pick just one, so I will go with all of the above.<br /> <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You walk the steps of your life, and always that dream beckons, that dream waits. You don’t know if it can ever be made real. You don’t know that, even should you somehow stumble upon it, you won’t find it less than it was, less than it could have been – if only you could have kept that distance, kept it just outside arm’s reach. For ever shining. For ever unsullied by the all-to-real flaws of your own making.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />The main thing that caught me of guard in <i>The Crippled God</i> was my feelings towards one of the characters. I had come to detest him so much throughout the other books, and at the end I found myself feeling only compassion for him. Erikson is always flipping the switch on the reader’s emotions, and he really caught me off guard with this one.<br /> <br />With <i>The Book of The Fallen</i> series wrapped up I look forward to the other books in the Malazan world from Erikson and Esslemont both. Sooner rather than later more than likely. For anyone searching for the most epic fantasy series out there you can look no further. This has it all and much much more. <br /> <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There shall be a Book and it shall be written by my hand. Wheel and seek the faces of a thousand gods! None can do what I can do! Not one can give voice to this holy creations. But this is not bravado For this, my Book of the Fallen, the only god worthy of its telling is the crippled one. The broken one. And has it not always been thus?<br />I never hid my hurts.<br />I never disguised my dreams.<br />And I never lost my way.<br />And only the fallen can rise again.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13152057876658988402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1204745016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204745016" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204745016?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781409010845" href="/book/show/13496864-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204745016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16447916406439600846"><b><em>The Crippled God</em> is a breathtaking conclusion to an outstanding series; <em>Malazan Book of the Fallen</em> is a masterpiece of its genre and has affirmed its place as my favourite epic grimdark fantasy series.</b><br/><br/><em>The Crippled God</em> didn't leave much room for breathers and I am sure this is the least amount of time I've spent finishing a novel in this series - the exception being <em>Gardens of the Moon</em>, which is the shortest book by far. I will also not spend much time relating about this final instalment, save t</span>
  <span id="freeText16447916406439600846" style="display:none"><b><em>The Crippled God</em> is a breathtaking conclusion to an outstanding series; <em>Malazan Book of the Fallen</em> is a masterpiece of its genre and has affirmed its place as my favourite epic grimdark fantasy series.</b><br /><br /><em>The Crippled God</em> didn't leave much room for breathers and I am sure this is the least amount of time I've spent finishing a novel in this series - the exception being <em>Gardens of the Moon</em>, which is the shortest book by far. I will also not spend much time relating about this final instalment, save that it was brilliantly handled with an emotionally exhausting, and wholly satisfying denouement. All the major open threads and even some smaller ones came together most compellingly. The very end of this book was of the most sublime symmetry to the beginning in <em>Gardens of the Moon</em>.<br /><br />The word <i>epic</i> does not even seem to do any justice to this expansive tale and the world in which it takes place. Erikson has skilfully crafted a story with such breadth and depth of worldbuilding and characterisation, and plot complexity, that it seriously challenges the readers. But, in spite of the work and commitment involved in finishing these ten books, it was also one of the most rewarding and fulfilling experiences I’ve ever had.<br /><br /><em>Malazan Book of the Fallen</em> is exquisitely soul-crushing and <i>yet</i> it can also make your heart soar - even when you're crying your eyes out. The narrative is crazily dense, filled with deep melancholic introspection and philosophical discourse, a mind-boggling number of intertwining storylines and a <i>massive</i> cast of characters. A stellar cast of characters for that matter, for whom any attempt to assuage emotional investment is futile. Believe me, Erikson will make you care – even for that minor side character that appeared for mere pages. He is a master at strumming powerful chords of emotion. So much grief, pain, sorrow and regret emanate from within its pages, beautifully tempered with empathy, compassion, kindness, loyalty and honour. These are stories of true friendships and enduring love; stories of the best of humanity in its darkest, and most dire, hours; delivered in a prose that is elegant and profound.<br /><br />The violence in this series is brutal and visceral, but never gratuitous. The battle and action scenes are in equal measures sweeping and intimate; cinematic scenes of clashing soldiers and sorcerous conflagration seen from a wide-angle, and combat sequences in close confines, moving from one squad, or an individual, to another. Although the level of power or ability commanded by some of the characters can be ridiculously off-the-charts, it is somehow appropriate in the context of this world. To me, that is part of the fun of reading <em>Malazan</em> which alleviated what seemed like hard work a lot of times. Admit it, badass characters are the most memorable and to partake in fantasy is to get swept away by the unreal awesomeness that you don't encounter in literary fiction.<br /><br />Having said that, while the story is told in a fantasy world, its allegory to our real world is staggeringly on point. To readers who scoff at the genre merely being escapism which never deals with real-life issues, I invite you to partake in this gritty epoch-spanning tale which echoes our actual bloody history – the horrors and grave errors perpetrated by humanity, repeated time and time again.<br /><br />I highly recommend anyone who loves fantasy, especially fans of grimdark, to read this series. Be patient, and you shall be rewarded.<br /><br />With choked emotions barely in check, I bid this world goodbye… for now. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>And now the page before us blurs.<br />An age is done. The book must close.<br />We are abandoned to history.<br />Raise high one more time the tattered standard<br />Of the Fallen. See through the drifting smoke<br />To the dark stains upon the fabric.<br />This is the blood of our lives, this is the<br />Payment of our deeds, all soon to be<br />Forgotten.<br />We were never what people could be.<br />We were only what we were.<br /><br />Remember us.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Series rating:</b>
</u><br /><br />Gardens of the Moon: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186511130" rel="nofollow noopener">5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />Deadhouse Gates: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744870" rel="nofollow noopener">5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />Memories of Ice: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744916" rel="nofollow noopener">5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />House of Chains: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744933" rel="nofollow noopener">4/5 stars</a>
</b><br />Midnight Tides: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2032772862" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />The Bonehunters: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744972" rel="nofollow noopener">5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />Reaper’s Gale: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744990" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />Toll The Hounds: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744997" rel="nofollow noopener">5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />Dust of Dreams: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204745011" rel="nofollow noopener">5/5 stars</a>
</b><br />The Crippled God: <b>5/5 stars.</b><br />Overall: <b>48/50 stars</b><br /><br /><strong>You can purchase the book from <u><a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Crippled-God-Steven-Erikson/9780765348876" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free Shipping)</a></u> | <u><a href="https://bookshop.org/books/the-crippled-god/9780765348876" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookshop.Org (Support Independent Bookstores</a> | <u><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Crippled-God-Book-Malazan-Fallen-ebook/dp/B004H1TQA8/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a></u> | <u><a href="https://www.amazon.co.uk/Crippled-God-Malazan-Book-Fallen/dp/0553813188/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a></u></u></strong><br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-2q5" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900630875?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer900630875" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3277342950539664014"><i>
  <b>‘The Bonehunters march alone, leaking blood with every step.’</b>
</i><br/><br/>There are so many bloody memorable lines in this book I need to collect them somewhere. Combined, they read like a movie trailer!<br/><br/><i>‘In that Malazan Book of the Fallen, the historians will write of our suffering, and they will speak of it as the suffering of those who served the Crippled God. As something … fitting. And for our seeming fanaticism they will dismiss all that we were, and think only of what we achieved. Or failed to achi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3277342950539664014" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘The Bonehunters march alone, leaking blood with every step.’</b>
</i><br /><br />There are so many bloody memorable lines in this book I need to collect them somewhere. Combined, they read like a movie trailer!<br /><br /><i>‘In that Malazan Book of the Fallen, the historians will write of our suffering, and they will speak of it as the suffering of those who served the Crippled God. As something … fitting. And for our seeming fanaticism they will dismiss all that we were, and think only of what we achieved. Or failed to achieve.<br />And in so doing, they will miss the whole fucking point.’</i><br /><br /><i>Shadowthrone hissed. ‘Well? Is that it?’<br />‘Is what it?’<br />‘That’s all you have to say? This is a momentous scene, you fat fool! This is where everything really, truly, finally begins! So squeeze the ale from your brain, mortal, and say something worthy of your kind. You stand before a god! Speak your eloquence for all posterity. Be profound!’ <br />‘Profound … huh.’ Temper was silent for a long moment, studying the cobbles of the alley mouth. And then he lifted his helmed head, faced Shadowthrone, and said, ‘Fuck off.’</i><br /><br /><i>You cannot kill us any more, but we can kill you, and so we shall. We are the sword of ancient memories. Memories of fire, memories of ice, memories of the pain you delivered upon us. I shall answer your crime. I shall be the hand of your utter annihilation.</i><br /><br /><i>I dream of returning, swords blazing with holy vengeance. I dream, Shadowthrone, of murdering every one of those fuckers. Is this what it means to be a god?</i><br /><br />And the most haunting one of them all<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘Quick Ben, we're soldiers of the Emperor. It's all we ever have been.’</i>
</b><br /><br />This has been a buddy read that's been ongoing for more than four <i>years</i>, with many casualties along the way (including myself for a short while). Big kudos to my friends Gavin &amp; Kaora for sticking with it until the very last book.<br /><br /><i>The Crippled God</i> is, in the end, one of the best instalments in the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> series. As shocking as that may seem to anyone who has attempted reading it, most of the plotlines, characters and themes do come together in the end.<br /><br />I am finding it extremely hard to sort through my thoughts enough to actually write a proper review for this last Malazan book. I suspect it (and the whole series) will inevitably warrant a reread, but until then, I will leave it at that.<br /><br />A fitting end to an exceptional series.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen reviews:</i>
</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271498" rel="nofollow noopener">Gardens of the Moon</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630799" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Gates</a><br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630812" rel="nofollow noopener">Memories of Ice</a><br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630817" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a><br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630830" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a><br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630838" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a><br />#7 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630842" rel="nofollow noopener">Reaper's Gale</a><br />#8 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630845" rel="nofollow noopener">Toll the Hounds</a><br />#9 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630849" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust of Dreams</a><br />#10 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630875" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crippled God</a></span>

  <span id="freeText556375481957075429" style="display:none">Re-read<br><br>I started a new job right about the time I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4703427.Dust_of_Dreams__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___9_" title="Dust of Dreams (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #9) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust of Dreams</a> which was 13 months ago. People who were reading these before all the books were published must have struggled mightily with this. <br>--------------<br>First read<br><br>Almost a year later and the 20th book total and 10th of the main series I’m done. What an epic ride that simply never disappointed. Not that I didn’t have doubts early in the series a few times. <br><br>But this series really has it all and I mean that literally. Elf’s, Dragons, Trolls, Ogres, shaper shifters, gods, magic of many forms and a system to back it up, religion, politics, humanity, violence, battles, war, love, history, ancient civilizations, action across better than five continents, divination, mysticism……I could go on and on. <br><br>And yet all that doesn’t begin to tell the story of why it’s great. The compassion weaved into the world and characters is beyond comparison. <br><br>Simply the greatest series I’ve ever read. <br><br>As for this book it’s really hard to say much without giving things away. I will say everything gets wrapped up. At the end there were tears in my eyes. So many characters had such crucial roles. <div id="review_1385425996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1385425996" />
    <a title="Ivan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31294609-ivan"><img alt="Ivan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605977265p2/31294609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1385425996?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivan" href="/user/show/31294609-ivan">Ivan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31294609-ivan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1385425996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1075294582764600249">And the journey ends. It's been a long one,after 10 books 9000 pages it's hard to say goodbye but like every Erikson's ending last pages of The Crippled god where epic and satisfying. It's impossible to say something about last book without spoilers so I won't. This will be review of the whole series.<br/><br/><br/> My journey started rough. Initially I DNF-ed first book @50%. It was because of enthusiasm of my GR friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9077850-molly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Molly</a> (sadly she hasn't been fully active in long time now) that I decided to give this se</span>
  <span id="freeText1075294582764600249" style="display:none">And the journey ends. It's been a long one,after 10 books 9000 pages it's hard to say goodbye but like every Erikson's ending last pages of The Crippled god where epic and satisfying. It's impossible to say something about last book without spoilers so I won't. This will be review of the whole series.<br /><br /><br /> My journey started rough. Initially I DNF-ed first book @50%. It was because of enthusiasm of my GR friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9077850-molly" rel="nofollow noopener">Molly</a> (sadly she hasn't been fully active in long time now) that I decided to give this series another go. On second try I managed to survive first book and seen potential. Rest of the series realizes that potential and Malazan book of fallen becomes everything people said it would be.<br /><br />And what is Malazan book of fallen? What makes it so unique?:<br /><br />Well it's combination of of heroic fantasy with heroes larger than life, gods, ancient evils and powerful magic and gimdark military fantasy with clash of big armies and how it affects common solider and people, all that spiced up with criticism of religion, capitalism but most of all strong anti-war message.What also makes this series unique is that it lacks classical protagonist. Instead, throughout the series we get several dozen of different PoVs and many more charters. Some have more screen time, some less but hey are all just pieces that paint much larger canvas. Canvas that has battles of gods, armies and mortals. Where magic, steel and gunpowder clash and heroes die.There are many story lines that intertwine and there are practically no wasted effort, everything that happens affects events later.Sometimes in next book, sometimes after six books. Since second and especially third book Erikson makes clear that nothing is sacred and that every character can die no matter how much you love him. Of course Martin is famous for doing that but Erikson's characters are much more epic and likable and I was genuinely sad when characters dies in Malazan book of fallen as Malazan contains some of most epic and intriguing characters in fantasy. Some deaths even broke my hearth. What is also unique is Erikson's writing style. He doesn't even try to go for something realistic and instead dialogues are rather epic and absurd. It's one of main things that made me DNF first book and indeed some dialogues there where very weird but as series progresses Erikson becomes much better at that style.<br /><br />Worldbuild:<br /><br />Well simply put there is no book that matches Malazan book of fallen in this regard. This is most fascinating, complex world with hundreds of thousands years of history. Erikson seem to be more efficient and puts more events, worldbuilding and characters per page than any other fantasy author<br /><br /><br />Flaws? Three worth mentioning.<br /><br />First, books in second half of the series sometimes drag on and felt bit too long.<br />Second, there is lot of philosophy in this book and sometimes it's intriguing and on point but sometimes it's boring and feels like verbal masturbation.<br />Third that comes from one of series's strengths. You need good memory or you need to read books in short span, preferably both. As mentioned above there are many characters and small events that affect story but not for several books. <br /><br />Conclusion:<br /><br />I didn't rate all books in the series 5 stars but as a whole this series deserves more than 5 stars and that's why it goes to favorites shelf. This is maybe the best fantasy series I read and something all other fantasy series will be measured against.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1075294582764600249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_416454941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416454941" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416454941?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416454941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer58277803432548390">The remaining Bonehunters continue their march through The Glass Desert (more on this desert thing later). The long-lost army of Ganoes Paran finally shows up, and I still have no clue what it was doing between the events in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/478951.The_Bonehunters__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___6_' title='The Bonehunters (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #6) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bonehunters</a> and this book; as to why it does what it did: I stopped wondering a long time ago - nobody gives an answer to this particular question in Malazan universe. A lot of forces gather in one place for the last showdown. Great battles are ensured. <br/><br/>As I mentioned ab</span>
  <span id="freeText58277803432548390" style="display:none">The remaining Bonehunters continue their march through The Glass Desert (more on this desert thing later). The long-lost army of Ganoes Paran finally shows up, and I still have no clue what it was doing between the events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/478951.The_Bonehunters__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___6_" title="The Bonehunters (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #6) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a> and this book; as to why it does what it did: I stopped wondering a long time ago - nobody gives an answer to this particular question in Malazan universe. A lot of forces gather in one place for the last showdown. Great battles are ensured. <br /><br />As I mentioned above, I gave up on trying figuring out the motivations of the main characters, as well as secondary ones. The 180 degrees plot twist in the middle of the book was lame, in my opinion; I cannot give any details without huge spoilers, but people who read this will know what I am talking about - as this twist came up suddenly and without any king of foreshadowing, or hint whatsoever. The battles are great and epic with good guys being rescued in the very last moment by deus ex machina type of intervention - all the time without failing. This is a really average book of the series, luckily the last one. One more thing to mention: the amount of unresolved plotlines boggles the mind. The people who were foreshadowed to play major role in the conflict resolution have around one page each where they do nothing really important. <br /><br />**************************<br /><br />The whole series review:<br /><br />Speaking about the whole series, I am relieved that I am finally finished it as well as disappointed. I expected a lot more from the hype surrounded the series. The first book blew me away, unfortunately the rest of the series failed to deliver the promise. I am glad I finished it, but I will never reread it: there are better books out there. Now that I finished, I need to change the rating of some of the books. My main complains:<br /><br />Nobody - and I do mean nobody - stays dead. Every person/being that died came back in one form or another, this means there is no emotional impact then a good guy dies: he/she will surely be back. I can only think of two exceptions of this rule: yes, in the whole series only two persons were gracious enough to remain dead.<br /><br />The author never explains motivations of any character, the reader has to guess all of it; this really began getting old around book 8. It is impossible to tell whether somebody did some heroic action on purpose, or because he happened to be in the wrong place at the wrong time.<br /><br />Despite the point above, we have a lot of inner monologues for any character, even ones who will disappear from the series forever without making any impact on the plot; everybody is a philosopher and miserable one at that. I would really like to see a happy person in Malazan universe, alas they do not exist; the kings and slaves are equally miserable.<br /><br />To continue the point above, there are a lot of characters who are not related to the plot in any sense, still we have to suffer their long inner monologues - and all the monologues are somewhat similar. Why do we have POVs of these people at all, except as a filler material? <br /><br />The last two points make books too long; what happened to editing? Every single book can be cut by two thirds without losing anything at all. Dear editors, when you charge money for your work, make sure you ACTUALLY FREAKIN' DO IT!!! If somebody could bother reducing the length of the series by half, the books would be really great; if somebody could manage to squeeze it all in a trilogy, the series would be a classic in genre, up there with The Lord of the Rings. As it is now, it is a torture to read most of the time. <br /><br />For the major parts of the books people do nothing (except for philosophy part) even though they know what is coming; nobody bothers to do anything in advance. When the shit finally hits the fan, people finally react doing great sacrifices - something that can be avoided if anybody bothered doing something before the crisis.<br /><br />Very frequent switching of POV, literally on every page, most notable in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55399.Gardens_of_the_Moon__The_Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___1_" title="Gardens of the Moon (The Malazan Book of the Fallen, #1) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Gardens of the Moon</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/938544.Toll_the_Hounds__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___8_" title="Toll the Hounds (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #8) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Toll the Hounds</a>. This one is my major complaint, this technique works only during intense battles, and for the rest of a book it is really bad. I always have to scan the page first to see whose POV I read about at the moment - as it is not always obvious, and then come back to the beginning of the page to read carefully.<br /><br />If there is a desert somewhere, people love wander in it aimlessly and endlessly. The moment I read about The Glass Desert in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4703427.Dust_of_Dreams__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___9_" title="Dust of Dreams (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #9) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust of Dreams</a>, I said: "Here it comes" and I was right. I imagine the Holy Desert Raraku looks like a downtown of a major city by the amount of people walking around in it. <br /><br />A lot of soldiers (Bridgeburners and Bonehunters) are completely indistinguishable from one another; they lack individuality: after all, they all think the same miserable philosophical thoughts. <br /><br />All in all, it is a major disappointment. What I am really scared of, is that from the immense popularity of the series some other fantasy writers will emulate this style. Oh well, there are a lot of older fantasy titles to read out there. I need to do some easy reading now, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/651146.The_Critique_of_Pure_Reason" title="The Critique of Pure Reason by Immanuel Kant" rel="nofollow noopener">The Critique of Pure Reason</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11038.Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant" rel="nofollow noopener">Immanuel Kant</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="58277803432548390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_130812179" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130812179" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130812179?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130812179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13999839826495890765">I started reading The Malazan Book of the Fallen just over four years ago, so finishing the final book of this ten volume epic is kind of a big deal for me. It's been a big part of my life in fact and it's odd to be at the end even though I know there are plenty more to go.<br/><br/>So you can imagine this series has had quite the impact on my life. When I go through my books to see which ones to sell or give away I call it "culling the nobility." It's pervasive. :) (wait, are emoticons allowed in Malazan</span>
  <span id="freeText13999839826495890765" style="display:none">I started reading The Malazan Book of the Fallen just over four years ago, so finishing the final book of this ten volume epic is kind of a big deal for me. It's been a big part of my life in fact and it's odd to be at the end even though I know there are plenty more to go.<br /><br />So you can imagine this series has had quite the impact on my life. When I go through my books to see which ones to sell or give away I call it "culling the nobility." It's pervasive. :) (wait, are emoticons allowed in Malazan reviews?)<br /><br />Gardens of the Moon was actually the first present my wife gave me for my birthday. We didn't have tons of money then (and still don't), but I couldn't have been happier receiving hours of entertainment and who'd've thunk how many hours it would end up being. Best. Wife. Ever.<br /><br />I was immediately drawn in and stunned by the vast imagination that is contained within those pages of even the first book and to come to the end it's even more amazing to see how far the story develops. At the moment, I'm even doing a reread of Gardens, which is like reading a completely new (and easily understandable) book. To see these characters early on and how far they come has been pretty fun already.<br /><br />The Crippled God actually has a lot of parallels with the first book and to warn you right now, we're headed into spoiler territory, but I assume if you've read this far, you've probably already read the whole series as it is anyway. <br /><br />In Gardens of the Moon, I loved the idea of that the whole plan was to release something of great power that would force your enemy to do battle and then your enemy would be weakened enough for you take on and beat. Yes, that is exactly how Erikson puts it, he's THAT good of a writer. :)<br /><br />Gardens uses this to weaken Anomander Rake, at least that's the goal and The Crippled God a similar tactic is used by the Gods Errastas, Sechul Lath, and Kilmandaros, but on a grander scale - releasing the Otatarial dragon to weaken Draconus among others.<br /><br />Both Gardens and TCG focus on the adjunct, although different adjuncts, and TCG mentions lots of events that happen in Gardens - talking about Lorn, the scene in the prologue to Gardens where Whiskeyjack talks to Ganoes, and Moon Spawn among others. We've come back around and I really appreciated these nods to the earlier work.<br /><br />My one major criticism of this series is that it tends to be a downer for much of the book. Words like "gritty" and "realistic" follow this series and while for the most part it's true, I have a hard time saying something is realistic when it ignores the good in people and society completely and focuses and has a cynical outlook on just about everything. That's not to say this series does, there are moments of awe-inspiring goodness, but they are few and far between. I prefer to think of it as this world and its gods are unredeemable, which is to say it's not that realistic. I don't think Erikson has claimed as such either, it's been the reviewers and fans.<br /><br />While I have had my difficulties with some of the previous volumes, they fail to take away from the fact that this series is incredible. Everything about it blows my mind and even some of the difficulties I've had I have been able to resolve. <br /><br />One of those being the fact that everyone, rich or poor, old or young, seems to have the need to philosophize. It was in a recent interview or podcast (I just can't quite remember which) that Erikson mentioned essentially that those who have been through the most are the wisest among us. This is something I had actually already known, but needed reacquainting with the idea. Not that I am wise, I've lived quite the privileged life even without any money, but I've talked with people who've been through a whole lot more than me, like an African refugee who left his country because his government was trying to kill him, and he and his family could tell you what life's all about. For some reason I didn't realize until then how much it applies to these characters in this book who are really suffering.<br /><br />There's really not much more to say than what I've said in my article, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40147581" rel="nofollow noopener">Why You Should Read The Malazan Book of the Fallen</a>, where I've attempted to convince people to read the series. In addition, I just don't have time to really get into a good review (yes, I'm studying for the bar...again), especially one that this series deserves, so below are a number of quotes with some commentary here and there throughout.<br /><br />-----------------<br /><br />The humor is still there, at times even Tehol makes "appearances" though not actually in person, which is always a good thing since he's arguably my favorite character in the entire series. Here's one instance I found terribly funny especially in my stage of life (baby twins and two year old):<br /><br />"'Then I'm going with you. My wife can go somewhere else. She keeps talking about babies but I don't want babies - they get in the way of having fun, and people who end up having them spend all day talking about how great it is, but they look miserable even when they're smiling. Or worse, there're those ones who think their baby is the God of Genius reborn and even its poo smells like flowers, and all they do is talk about them for ever and ever and it's so boring I want to run away...' <br />'A rather uncharitable view, Ublala.' <br />'I don't give nothing for free, that's for sure. Whole people disappear when a baby arrives. Poof! Where'd they go? Oh, I know, they're crawling around making baby noises. It makes me sick." He ducked the rock Ralata threw at him..." p. 522<br /><br />But of course, Erikson delves deeper as well, leaving you to ponder your existence, to see the futilities, the baseness, but also very often he leads you to hope:<br /><br />"I could run until I wear out. Every joint, every bone and every muscle. I could run until my heart groans older than its years, and finally bursts. <br />I could damn the poets and make the metaphor real. We are all self-destructive. It is integral to our nature. And we will run even when there's nowhere to run to, and nothing terrible to run from. Why? Because to walk is just as meaningless. It just takes longer." p. 389<br /><br />This took me a few times, but it's dead on:<br /><br />"'"When wisdom drips blood fools stand triumphant."'" p. 628 (Brother Diligence quoting Gothos' Folly)<br /><br />I recently moved from a smaller town to a big city and this one really got me thinking:<br /><br />"He wondered at all those lives, the way few would meet the gazes of their fellows, as if crowds demanded wilful anonymity, when the truth was they were all in it together - all these people, facing much the same struggles, the same fears. And yet, it seemed, each one was determined to survive them alone, or with but a few kin and friends offering paltry allegiance. Perhaps they each believed themselves unique, like a knot-stone in the centre of the world's mill wheel, but the truth was there were very few who could truly make claim to such a pivotal existence." p. 749<br /><br />It's sad we tend to look away or even attempt to work things out on our own when it's unnecessary. Why can't we just help each other along through this existence instead of ignoring, judging, and leaving people behind. My wife says that this is why things like the shootings in Sandy Hook happened - people just don't get enough love in their lives. I can't say I disagree.<br /><br />I fitting summary of the series title and it's meaning:<br /><br />"In that Malazan Book of the Fallen, the historians will write of our suffering, and they will speak of it as the suffering of those who served the Crippled God. As something ... fitting. And for our seeming fanaticism they will dismiss all that we were, and think only of what we achieved. Or failed to achieve." p. 330 <br /><br />Here's one I found particularly humbling, I didn't know Erikson even read my blog:<br /><br />"Gesler took her face in his hands and kissed her hard on the lips. 'Teach these lizards, Kalyth, only the best in us humans. Only the best.'" p. 771<br /><br />Another very interesting quote that I heartily agree with:<br /><br />"'It is not enough to wish for a better world for the children. It is not enough to shield them with ease and comfort, to make the future's world a better one, then we curse our own children. We leave them a misery they do not deserve; we leave them a host of lessons unearned.'" p. 783<br />-----------------<br /><br />The Crippled God is a fitting ending to quite possibly my favorite series of all time. It's more epic than I could have ever imagined and the action does not disappoint especially in the end of each book. Neither does Erikson's ability to drag emotions from you whether you want it or not. The Malazan Book of the Fallen will be the high water mark for epic fantasy for years to come, it's brutal, it's genius, it's an experience unlike anything else.<br /><br />5 out of 5 Stars (A Masterpiece of Epic Proportions!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13999839826495890765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1200411716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200411716" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200411716?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200411716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13206835516096708160">Simple review. If you have gotten this far you do not need an introduction. If you have made it this far then you do not want me to spoil the plot. People have analysed that the ending of the series is weak. I completely disagree. This is up there with Deadhouse Gates, Memories Of Ice and Midnight Tides. Everything is written perfectly. Poetic. I cared about all the point of view characters. Even the storylines I did not care about too much in the prior instalment Dust Of Dreams, such as the Sha</span>
  <span id="freeText13206835516096708160" style="display:none">Simple review. If you have gotten this far you do not need an introduction. If you have made it this far then you do not want me to spoil the plot. People have analysed that the ending of the series is weak. I completely disagree. This is up there with Deadhouse Gates, Memories Of Ice and Midnight Tides. Everything is written perfectly. Poetic. I cared about all the point of view characters. Even the storylines I did not care about too much in the prior instalment Dust Of Dreams, such as the Shake come to fruition here and you understand the necessity for the journey. You need to just read it. There are so many great scenes combining a huge amount of the big players that we have been following over what is a span of about ten years in this saga. Characters meet each other again after say 8-9 books apart and some of those moments are heart-wrenching. You will know the points when you get to them. There are so many amazing stand out dramatic scenes. A lot of the plots are wrapped up but you will still leave with so many questions. Ublula and Draconus are up there with Tehol and Bugg for their comedy gold. Forget this review. Just read this is you haven't already. Fiction especially fantasy will not compare to me anymore. I feel like part of my life is over now completing it. Take care all. Peace x.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youandibooks.wordpress.com">www.youandibooks.wordpress.com</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_1877172331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1877172331" />
    <a title="Michael Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt"><img alt="Michael Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513347398p2/51188905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1877172331?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Britt" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt">Michael Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51188905-michael-britt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877172331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14773154829346015143"><b>"And now the page before us blurs. An age is done. The book must close."</b><br/><br/>Wow, all things considered, that was the best ending I could've hoped for for a series so tragic. I'll share my thoughts on this book and then the series as a whole. Keeping it spoiler free, per usual. <br/><br/>After the slow pace of Dust of Dreams, this installment seemed more fast paced than the other books. I think going in with low expectations helped, as well. Even though we didnt get resolution on <i>everything</i>, we still got closu</span>
  <span id="freeText14773154829346015143" style="display:none"><b>"And now the page before us blurs. An age is done. The book must close."</b><br /><br />Wow, all things considered, that was the best ending I could've hoped for for a series so tragic. I'll share my thoughts on this book and then the series as a whole. Keeping it spoiler free, per usual. <br /><br />After the slow pace of Dust of Dreams, this installment seemed more fast paced than the other books. I think going in with low expectations helped, as well. Even though we didnt get resolution on <i>everything</i>, we still got closure on so many other things. I did feel like some characters were under utilized, one in particular, in these last 2 novels. While I was disappointed that we didnt see him much, Erikson more than made up for it with some of my older favorites. The OG's, if you will.<br /><br />There's not really much I can say about this novel without spoilers, so I'll conclude with this: this is a book that ramps up the epicness of this series from a 10 to a 20. And he also gives us a conclusion that is as fulfilling as you can hope for without sacrificing the tragic theme for sake of having a happy ending just because. <br /><br /><b>"What's three and a half million words between friends?- from Acknowledgements</b><br /><br />Now, on to my thoughts on this series as whole, since this wraps up almost all of the plots. There are so many. So many that I'm pretty sure I missed a lot of what others might have seen clearly.<br /><br />This is by far the most epic series in all of Fantasy, in every sense of the word and in every aspect. The cast rivals any series out there. I can't recall any series to use a cast this big. And with this big of a cast comes so many different story arcs. All of this is my favorite part of the series, but it was also the focal point of many of my frustrations. Especially in Dust of Dreams. Sometimes you won't see a character til 3, 4 or even 5 books later. Usually that's not a big problem, but keeping track of a cast this size can get pretty exhausting. I had to forgo the Dramatis Personae and very carefully wade through the wiki.<br /><br />This is the most rewarding series I have yet to read. While it gets frustrating having to remember who is doing what, the payoffs from all that work far outweighs any frustrations. While most of the books have a relatively slow beginning, the payoff you get, when you finally get there has never disappointed. <br /><br />Now, onto my favorite part of any series, the characters. One of the things I love most about this series, in particular, are the characters. More so their development. I also love how grey most of the cast is. Some do some terrible things, but for reasons you cant quite comprehend just then. I also love how he wrote most of his female characters. Most of the time I couldn't discern the males from the females unless there were either anatomical descriptors or a he/she put after the sentence. We got some really bad ass females in this series, too. <br /><br />All the different plots and story arcs were interesting. Or they were to ne, at least. I never found myself disliking the arcs for any specific race. Although, the K'Chain Che'Malle were among my favorites, by far. <br /><br />That's really about all I have to say regarding this book and the series. All-in-all, i highly recommend this series to anyone looking for something that's more epic than any Epic Fantasy series out. Plus, <b>IT'S AN EPIC FANTASY SERIES THAT IS FINISHED</b>. Which finishing a series seems like a hard thing to do, so I felt I should mention it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14773154829346015143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
