<div id="review_2309354857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2309354857" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2309354857?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781409010845" href="/book/show/13496864-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Epic Fantasy readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2309354857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2123978170987963298"><b>
  <i>Trust me when I say this will be the biggest the world has ever seen, bigger even than the chaining of the Crippled God.<br/><br/>There are too many rogue players in this game. Icarium. Draconus. The First Sword of the T’lan Imass. Olar Ethil, Silchas Ruin, Tulas Shorn, Kilava – even Gruntle, the Mortal Sword of Treach. And now the Eleint, and how many dragons have come or are coming through the gate? A hundred? A thousand? Oh, and the Elder Gods: Errastas, the past Master of the Tiles, and Kilmandaros</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText2123978170987963298" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Trust me when I say this will be the biggest the world has ever seen, bigger even than the chaining of the Crippled God.<br /><br />There are too many rogue players in this game. Icarium. Draconus. The First Sword of the T’lan Imass. Olar Ethil, Silchas Ruin, Tulas Shorn, Kilava – even Gruntle, the Mortal Sword of Treach. And now the Eleint, and how many dragons have come or are coming through the gate? A hundred? A thousand? Oh, and the Elder Gods: Errastas, the past Master of the Tiles, and Kilmandaros and her son.....<br /><br />‘Let’s just add the K’Chain Che’Malle and the Jaghut, and oh, we should probably mention Hood himself – no longer dragging the Throne of Death by one ankle. And who knows how many slavering fanatics of the Wolves of Winter! And what about the Crippled God himself – will he go quietly?</i>
</b><br /><br />That quote sums up the whole book, its the final stand for everybody. This series is now my favourite series of all time, I doubt any fantasy series can live up to this series.<br /><br /><u>World building and Writing </u><br />The world building is out of this world, its so well depicted, The glass desert is even worse than anyone would have anticipated and Steven Erickson still wowed me. Do not even get me started on the writing, they are like a zillion POVs, I have to admit it took a while to get used to, after that it was a piece of cake. Everyone that survived the past 9 books are all in this, sadly not all of them made it to the ending of the book. *sniffles*<br /><br /><b>
  <i> "Grieving had nothing to do with the ones gone, and everything to do with the ones left behind. We feel the absences in our life like open wounds, and they never really close, no matter how many years pass."</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br /><b> The Malazans</b><br />The Bonehunters survivors after the incident with the K'chain Nahruk are still trying to cross the glass desert which has never been crossed in like forever, they lost most of the company, to thirst but the few survivors were still willing to die to do what needs to be done. To fight the Forkrall Assail who is determined to end humanity, then there's the thing with the crippled god that is a major spoiler.<br /><br /><b> The Adjunt's allies</b><br />They include the Letherris, Bolkando, the grey helms, the burned tears and The K'chain Chemelle, yea them. These ones took a shortcut to get to the enemies, but even them lost a sustainable number of their company.<br /><br /><br /><b>T'lan Imass</b><br />They are also here, they are just marching in the glass desert, they were all summoned here to come fight a war they know nothing about. Lots of the Imass here have POVs so we know what is going on in their head and its so sad, but it all paid off at the end,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Fener died and his blood made them flesh and blood again, saldy it happened during battle so they sustained mortal injury and died, but Onoos Toolan survived <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> though more than half of them died.<br /><br /><b> The Tiste andiis and Liosan</b><br />The pretentious liosans wants to continue their war on the andiis, due to the rip in the realm, the same rip that brought the Eleint to this world. But the andiis are not in Kharkanas, the people they met were formidable fighters, they held the gate.<br /><br /><b>The Snake</b><br />These children will make you weep at the same time be happy for the life you have. They are brave courageous and just refused to give up, I hope they get the best out of life.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>I am as true as anything you have ever seen. A dying child, abandoned by the world. And I say this: there is nothing truer. Nothing.<br />Flee from me if you can. I promise I will haunt you. This is my only purpose now, the only one left to me. I am history made alive, holding on but failing.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>The Assail</b><br />These is the race that judged humans unworthy to be alive. They are ready to do anything to annihilate humans. They magic and warren is so ancient that they can control not only mind but body. What they did not anticipate is human's will to live.<br /><br /><b>The Elient</b><br />The gate is once again open, the last time the dragons were in this world they destroyed lots of continents and now they are back. T'am the mother of dragons is also on her way, not to mention Otataral that negates magic and lay waste to anywhere she passes.<br /><br /><b>The gods</b> <br />The gods in this series are worse than the greek gods, they love to meddle so much, they all want one thing, more power. <br />They are willing to use humans to get what they want, its doesn't matter whether or not the people make it. To say they are selfish is an understatement.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>We are sickened by the unknown, but knowledge can prove poisonous. And drifting lost between the two is no better.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2123978170987963298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2972632540" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8531296954511018333"><b>Chapter 24:</b> Only the fallen can rise again.* May, but this series has fallen (and none of the epilogues changed that). <br/><br/><b>Chapter 23:</b> Oh no. What do you mean "DIFFERENT TOES?!" You just rendered a couple of hundreds of pages an entirely meaningless waste of time on my part. Seriously. If I quit now, nobody is going to blame me. <br/><br/><b>Chapter 22:</b> Guess what, I can see the light at the end of this tunnel! <br/><br/><b>Chapter 21:</b> Tavore Paran, let it be known that you are the only reason for my perseverance. <br/><br/><b>Chapter 20</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8531296954511018333" style="display:none"><b>Chapter 24:</b> Only the fallen can rise again.* May, but this series has fallen (and none of the epilogues changed that). <br /><br /><b>Chapter 23:</b> Oh no. What do you mean "DIFFERENT TOES?!" You just rendered a couple of hundreds of pages an entirely meaningless waste of time on my part. Seriously. If I quit now, nobody is going to blame me. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 22:</b> Guess what, I can see the light at the end of this tunnel! <br /><br /><b>Chapter 21:</b> Tavore Paran, let it be known that you are the only reason for my perseverance. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 20:</b> Honorary marine. That is nice.<br /><br /><b>Chapter 19:</b> Yes, yes. At last, this behemoth of a plot starts showing some tentative signs of life. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 18:</b> Oh, NOW are the oldies popping up out of atrophied plots? Well, finally.<br /><br /><b>Chapter 17:</b> [two months later] This book might yet bee a death of me. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 16:</b> Honestly, I expect Greta Thunberg to have her own POV any time now.<br /><br /><b>Chapter 15:</b> At this point I just hope everybody dies in the next chapter to ease their pain. And mine. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 14:</b> Never can have too many kittens, can we? Precisely, sir. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 13:</b> What do I care about all these new protagonists who popped up a book or two ago? Nothing! Give me the old ones! I miss #sorrynotsorry and the whole lot I loved in the first three books that somehow got abandoned along the way.<br /><br /><b>Chapter 12:</b> I am trying to remember what this chapter was about and why it matters. Alas, I fail. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 11:</b> With all this anti-civilisational anti-human rubbish strewn across those chapters, I am truly surprised this series is not a holy book of Extinction Rebellion. I expect they would gob it up without editing. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 10:</b> Confession time: I skip all the poems. Tolkien this is not. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 9:</b> [the pages go by] <br /><br /><b>Chapter 8:</b> I can see what you are doing here with the Dark and the Light. I can see and I don't like it, Mr Erikson. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 7:</b> Truly, my trial of going through all of this is... unwitnessed. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 6:</b> I always knew it was not healthy to be a dragon. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 5:</b> Something seems to be happening. Or planning/plotting/scheming/walking to be happening. But hard to say what. Also, it is hardly interesting. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 4:</b> A kindly fisted army. Some genuine enjoyment at last. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 3:</b> [snip! snip! snip!] That's me mentally cutting huge, redundant chunks of this "story". <br /><br /><b>Chapter 2:</b> I don't really know who half of the cast is at this stage. I barely care for the other half. <br /><br /><b>Chapter 1:</b> The Adjunct. I am here for the Adjunct. <br /><br /><b>Prologue:</b> I cannot believe I am here already. <br /><br /><b>* I am not going to even pretend that I could in any way give a pale shadow of justice to this book or indeed a whole series in a proper review.</b> There are many better than me, here on Goodreads (and many of those I'm lucky to have among my friends), who managed to grasp and convey the sheer brilliance of what awaits those who open the Malazan Book of the Fallen. <b>All I can give you is a chapter breakdown of how this book crippled me forever.</b><br /><br />The Malazan Book of the Fallen:<br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577764482" rel="nofollow noopener">Gardens of the Moon</a> ★★★★★<br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277757848" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Gates</a> ★★★★★<br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2379526635" rel="nofollow noopener">Memories of Ice</a> ★★★★★<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437981495" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a> ★★★★★<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2516054197" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a> ★★★★★<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2596107471" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a> ★★★★★<br />7. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2652025092" rel="nofollow noopener">Reaper's Gale</a> ★★★★☆<br />8. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2784628226" rel="nofollow noopener">Toll the Hounds</a> ★★★★★<br />9. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2905503793?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust of Dreams</a> ★★★☆☆ (and the third star is a testament to my generosity)</span>

<div id="review_2697399003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2697399003" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2697399003?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2697399003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9937971984714020952">I'm not going to say too much about this final instalment of the Malazan Book of the Fallen series. Mostly because I've prattled on long enough in my previous 9 reviews about all the reasons why this is such a great series. If you have made it to this 10th book chances are you already know about them as well! I do think The Crippled God was a satisfying conclusion to the series and that on the whole Malazan is one of the two true epics the fantasy genre has to offer. The other series being WoT a</span>
  <span id="freeText9937971984714020952" style="display:none">I'm not going to say too much about this final instalment of the Malazan Book of the Fallen series. Mostly because I've prattled on long enough in my previous 9 reviews about all the reasons why this is such a great series. If you have made it to this 10th book chances are you already know about them as well! I do think The Crippled God was a satisfying conclusion to the series and that on the whole Malazan is one of the two true epics the fantasy genre has to offer. The other series being WoT and Malazan probably tops that in terms of scope and epic feel!<br /><br />In terms of storyline this was a direct continuation from the 9th book with the Malazan's and their various allies heading to Kolanse for an epic battle. As far as the Gods and Ascendants were concerned they were all heading to Kolanse as well for and epic Convergence! <br /><br />It all made for compelling reading. The Bonehunters featured heavily, as one might expect, but I was happy to see the return of a lot of our favourites from the earlier books even if the likes of K'rul and Kruppe did just pop up in cameos. <br /><br />As always Erikson did a good job of balancing the social commentary and story. I feel like his musings were a little grim and he botched the delivery of a few relevant points he was trying to make a couple of times but that on the whole I felt like his observations were fun and enhanced my enjoyment of the story. <br /><br />Most of the reason why this final instalment of the Malazan Book of the Fallen series was so satisfying was because Erikson got the balance spot on. This was a dark book with tons or war and violence but I feel like Erikson still managed to offer a satisfying balance between the tragedy and triumph and the hope and despair within the story. The ending was also very good! Both the final mega convergence and the wrap up were fun. The absolute toughest thing to get right is the ending of a long running series so credit to Erikson for delivering a truly satisfying and fitting ending to this series! <br /><br />I think that is all I have to say. This was a great ending to a great series and thankfully I'm not done with it yet as I still have a bunch of Esslemont's companion Malazan books to go. <br /><br />Rating: 5 stars. Not my favourite book in the Malazan series but it was still very good and well worth 5 stars. It was a continuation of the 9th book in many ways but it also eliminated a lot of that instalments main flaws. <br /><br />Audio Note: Michael Page did a great job as always. Between Lister, Page, and Banks I've listened to a few different authors take on Malazan and am happy to say all three narrators do an excellent job and jumping between them was surprisingly smooth and not at all jarring! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9937971984714020952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_359694354" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/359694354" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/359694354?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10697676-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359694354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6684944153318857767"><br/><u>
  <b>Reread Review</b>
</u><br/><br/>Some six months after reading this book the first time I, along with some other hardcore Malazan veterans, with a lot of virgin Malazan readers in tow undertook the epic task of rereading the entire Malazan Book of the Fallen series. Sixteen months later here we are, finished again. Well done.<br/><br/>I'm not going to change my initial review of the book itself because I feel what I have already written(below) is sufficient for that purpose. What I really want to comment on is the experi</span>
  <span id="freeText6684944153318857767" style="display:none"><br /><u>
  <b>Reread Review</b>
</u><br /><br />Some six months after reading this book the first time I, along with some other hardcore Malazan veterans, with a lot of virgin Malazan readers in tow undertook the epic task of rereading the entire Malazan Book of the Fallen series. Sixteen months later here we are, finished again. Well done.<br /><br />I'm not going to change my initial review of the book itself because I feel what I have already written(below) is sufficient for that purpose. What I really want to comment on is the experience of rereading the entire series. Having a look at my initial comments here I see that reading this series the first time around was at once very rewarding, but also quite frustrating at times. I am happy to report that the reread was a far superior experience to the extent that I would say the reward for reading this series is in being able to read it again.<br /><br />A lot of my frustrations in not being able to connect the dots initially to a lot of the plot arcs turned into the satisfaction of discovering nuggets of missing links that had eluded me, and possibly would always have eluded me except I had undertaken to search for them retrospectively. On top of this was the added enjoyment that could only come from the discussion and sharing of ideas with new and old Malazan readers alike at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/85396" rel="nofollow noopener">The Malazan Fallen Book Club</a>. I think this series, more than a lot of epic fantasy out there lends itself well to in depth group analysis and conversation. I think that the result of both the density of content in the books as well as Erikson's use of the unreliable narrator. I think there is only one or maybe two times in the whole series where we get an impartial omniscient view of the lay of the land. Most of the narration otherwise comes from POV characters who are imperfect and have an incomplete and often flawed perspective of what is actually true in the story. As such, you can have a single event described in different and often contradictory ways depending on who is telling a story. As such, even right at the end, there is no consensus of interpretations among members of the book club - which I like even if everyone else is wrong. <br /><br />I think Erikson has succeeded in simulating somewhat the experience of archaeologists and anthropologists(of whom he is one) who must try to put together pieces of the past from fragments of scrolls, and ancient ruins, and bits of bone. Like all stories of the past we attempt to reconstruct, the evidence does not necessarily speak for itself (contrary to what Grissom on CSI says) - all evidence, particularly of the past, is interpreted through the filters of our individual biases and opinions and experience. And so we have had a book club that looks at the same book, the same evidence, and yet at times comes up with a variety of interpretations that has made for some very satisfying interaction. <br /><br />I would also like to think that we have left behind a useful resource for other readers of the series who come after us - I'm not sure of anywhere else online where there is a separate non-spoilery thread for each and every chapter for each and every book of the whole Malazan Book of the Fallen series, so that regardless of where someone is in the series they can <i>safely</i> look for answers that may have eluded them.<br /><br />To those Malazan fans who were there from the beginning, to those who joined us on the way, to those who contributed for a portion of the way - I salute you all. Thank you for marching with me through the oases as well the wastelands of this series and making the journey all that more enjoyable.<br /><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Initial review</b>
</u><br /><br /><br />Here ends my epic read of an epic series. I consider the completion of these 10 books as a personal achievement. To say I have enjoyed the series would be over simplistic. Certainly there have been some very memorable moments and some very memorable characters throughout the series. But there have also been a plethora of generic and non interesting characters. There have been story lines/arcs that have been fast paced - but also a lot of story arcs that appear painfully slow, pointless and uninteresting. The writing style also is difficult at times with Erikson having the annoying habit of assuming the reader should know or remember small tidbits or clues to puzzles so that when the final piece is delivered there is no need for him to describe the final picture. And often he doesn't. While this can be very rewarding at those times when I figure stuff out on my own, there are a lot of times when I'm not sure if I got everything or if I missed something on the way.<br /><br />Having said all this, I have yet to read a book in the series where I felt I wasted my time. The battle and action sequences are intense. The world building and magic system is generally consistent and interesting. And the interesting characters are really interesting. I will hold on to a lot of memorable moments like Quick Ben outwitting Korbal Broach and Bauchelain, Anomander Rake and his sky keep, Kruppe moving deftly through the streets of Darujhistan using his immense powers to steal and consume cakes from venders, Ganoes Paran who became "Master of the Deck," Fiddler and his explosives, Kalam the Assassin, Whiskey Jack, Icarium Lifestealer, Tehol and Bugg, and there are more. <br /><br />Reflecting on the series now I remember nearly giving up on the first book thinking that there were very few characters I cared about - but by this last book I have found myself attached to many of The Fallen and so take a moment to shed a tear for comrades lost either to battles within the pages or to those I have had to leave behind to fates I will never learn . . .<i>sniff</i>.<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Spoilers for anyone who hasn't got this far yet</b>
</i><br /><br />But enough of that. In this last book of the series we rejoin Tavore and the Bonehunters on a gruelling march across a glassy waste to cheat the gods and to right an ancient injustice. By the end of the previous book we have an almost complete picture now of the plan for the Crippled God - a plan hatched by Shadowthrone and Cotillion along with Rake, Hood and later on Ganoes Paran. The plan was simple - just release the Crippled God from his chains so he can go back to where he came from. What's so hard about that? Forkrul Assail for one. An elder race who intend to feed off the Crippled gods power to bring an end to the universe. And maybe we throw in some Elder god has-beens who intend to release the Otateral Dragon and bring an end to the world. <br /><br />So did Shadow have a brilliant plan for countering all this magic and universe ending power? Well that's what the mere mortals are for. With blood and steel and a special one finger salute for anything with the word "elder" or/and "god" in front of it. <br /><br />4 stars from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6684944153318857767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13545290558984105497" style="display:none">There were three different times in the last forty pages where I was emarrassingly sobbing. Thank god I was home alone and avoided having to explain myself to people that don't read. Explaining the impact of this stunning conclusion to those that need their entertainment spoon fed to them is beyond my capacity. But you guys get it, and for that I'm grateful. <br />As others have stated sharing any favorite parts would be spoilers for earlier books so I wont go there but the bringing together of all that came before is ten to fifteen minute standing ovation worthy and maybe the satisfying in terms of how everything concluded. Ive only re-read maybe six or seven books my whole life but the complexity and flat out funness of this story demands a second go around to which I am very much looking forard to. <br />All ten books took roughly seven months to read and every book is a step above everything else in any category IMHO.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9566376886298188709">Wow. Just wow. It took me a long time to get to this point, but it was so worth it. I can't say much about the book itself because I would just have to mark the whole review as a spoiler, but what I will say is Erikson has truly created a masterpiece. <br/><br/>Having so many characters and plot-lines makes it really difficult to tie together, and sometimes authors flop at the end or just never finish.   <span id="freeText9566376886298188709" style="display:none">Wow. Just wow. It took me a long time to get to this point, but it was so worth it. I can't say much about the book itself because I would just have to mark the whole review as a spoiler, but what I will say is Erikson has truly created a masterpiece. <br /><br />Having so many characters and plot-lines makes it really difficult to tie together, and sometimes authors flop at the end or just never finish. Erikson is not one of those authors. He has one of the largest worlds, if not the largest, in fantasy fiction and yet he perfectly finishes this amazingly epic series.<br /><br />If you're reading this review and you haven't yet started Malazan, now is the time to jump into Erikson's vast and beautiful world. Starting <i>Gardens of the Moon</i> is a daunting task: a huge book that is super confusing with 9 more super huge books to follow. I'm here to tell you that it is all worth it. This book, and this series, now proudly sits at the top of my favourites list and will likely not move from its position.</span>

I loved, I laughed, I cried...every book in this series was amazing. I feel that no other series will ever measure up to this. It's a world I have been obsessed with. I'm already wanting to reread all of it. These lines from the Never Ending Story sum up perfectly how I feel now that it's over. <br/><br/><i>If you have never wept bitter tears because a wonderful story has come to an end and you mus</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14561811379204390103" style="display:none">It's been 6 months, 10 books, 8,000+ pages and 3.3 million words...The Malazan Book of the Fallen was worth it. I loved, I laughed, I cried...every book in this series was amazing. I feel that no other series will ever measure up to this. It's a world I have been obsessed with. I'm already wanting to reread all of it. These lines from the Never Ending Story sum up perfectly how I feel now that it's over. <br /><br /><i>If you have never wept bitter tears because a wonderful story has come to an end and you must take your leave of the characters with whom you have shared so many adventures, whom you have loved and admired, for whom you have hoped and feared, and without whose company life seems empty and meaningless. If such things have not been part of your own experience, you probably won't understand...</i><br /><br />It's the first time for me any book series has 100% delivered on every book and had an ending that was heartbreaking yet hopeful and mostly perfect. No major loose ends, no feeling of being let down - everything was as it should be. Probably the most daunting series of books I've ever read - and I've never loved anything more. <br /><br />I'll end the same as Erikson did...<br /><br /><i>And now the page before us blurs.<br />An age is done. The book must close.<br />We are abandoned to history.<br />Raise high one more time the tattered standard<br />Of the Fallen.         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765310101" href="/book/show/8722535-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5024825-traci?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5024825-traci?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168757883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7880821202397049795">...OMG...<br/>Standing ovation, bow,...grovel.<br/>I wish I could thank Steven Erikson for writing this series. It is exactly what I have been searching for. Heroic fantasy for your brain. <br/>I can however thank those of you here on goodreads. For some reason I had never heard of these books until I joined. And I might never have on my own. My book shelf would have remained incomplete. I'm serious. I have been reading fantasy for a long time and have seen favorites come and go. Truthfully I've been a little </span>
  <span id="freeText7880821202397049795" style="display:none">...OMG...<br />Standing ovation, bow,...grovel.<br />I wish I could thank Steven Erikson for writing this series. It is exactly what I have been searching for. Heroic fantasy for your brain. <br />I can however thank those of you here on goodreads. For some reason I had never heard of these books until I joined. And I might never have on my own. My book shelf would have remained incomplete. I'm serious. I have been reading fantasy for a long time and have seen favorites come and go. Truthfully I've been a little jealous over readers who have "the book". You know what I mean. The favorite above all favorites. Well, I don't think I need to be any longer. <br />Now for my review I suppose.<br /><br />Book 5 stars (6!)<br />Series 5 stars (8!!!)<br />After 10,267 pages the story finally comes into focus. It combines what is great about the previous books. Especially when the focus is on the Bonehunters and Bridgeburners. It reminded me a bit of the fast pace of Gardens of the Moon. But with more clarity. With more attachment to the characters. With more investment in the story. I loved the end. It's not all happy. Not all tragedy. There are even some things left unresolved. I cried a little. Okay, maybe more than a little. I was holding up quite well until the last scene with Fiddler and Hedge. I laughed a little. And I never knew what to expect next. A very satisfying conclusion.<br /><br />This series takes a certain commitment of the reader. And it's not for everyone. It seems you either love or hate it. My advice for new readers is to keep notes on character names. This was three fourths of all problems I ran into personally. And I will be doing this when I do a reread. Probably sometime within this year.<br /><br />Favorite character without a doubt Fiddler. I usually go for the "cool" characters. The Kalam. Quick Ben. Cotillion. Rake. But somehow with all these unique interesting characters the one that won my heart was the average soldier. The reluctant hero who was uncomfortable with his role. One of my favorite parts (there were many) was the Bonehunters "last" march. Perfectly written.<br /><br />Also loved Gesler and Stormy. Icarium and Mappo (I don't "mind" how this ended but I would still like to know more about this duo). Toc the younger (his last scene was another teary moment). Onos T'oolan. Tehol. Bugg. Brys. Can't forget Bottle. Onrack. I missed Trull. I would've loved to see him again. I was left wanting more of Karsa Orlong.<br /><br />I loved the two epilogues. Korlat and Whiskey Jack. Another teary moment. And how the book ended in an almost full circle moment.<br /><br />I'm at a lost on what to read next. I'm glad to have finished but sad to be leaving. Even though I know I will return. Probably sooner than I am thinking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7880821202397049795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10487271323173598450">When you pick up a book, you want to experience a story. When you pick up a High Fantasy saga, you want to be transported into another world, a fantastic world, and you want to submerge yourself in it.<br/>Normally, when reading Dark/Grimdark Fantasy, you don't expect the book to make you cry... but Malazan does. It keeps hitting you in the ground until you cry, it gives you a moment of freedom, so you can experience happiness and cry because of it... and then it proceeds with kicking you some more.<br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText10487271323173598450" style="display:none">When you pick up a book, you want to experience a story. When you pick up a High Fantasy saga, you want to be transported into another world, a fantastic world, and you want to submerge yourself in it.<br />Normally, when reading Dark/Grimdark Fantasy, you don't expect the book to make you cry... but Malazan does. It keeps hitting you in the ground until you cry, it gives you a moment of freedom, so you can experience happiness and cry because of it... and then it proceeds with kicking you some more.<br />And you know what? It's FREAKING AWESOME!!!!<br />I have never felt this hooked to a story. Or at least i haven't felt like this in a LONG while.<br /><br />It's a LONG journey. Long, complicated, treacherous, filled with different branches, with sorrow, friendship, camaraderie, hope, compassion.<br />This saga has been with me throughout this whole year, with it's ups and downs, and i am having a hard time figuring out how things are gonna be now that it's done... it feels, weird.<br />But the odyssey was worth it... it was long, it was hard, but it was needed. Your mind will be blown away, you will experience awe and it will be hard to get back to the genre after this beauty, 'cause it will be hard to top.<br /><br />This is a beautiful saga, and you need to read it. Don't be afraid, delve into it, it's worth it.</span>

<div id="review_142613930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142613930" />
    <a title="Captain Sir Roddy, R.N. (Ret.)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret"><img alt="Captain Sir Roddy, R.N. (Ret.)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453308913p2/2482609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142613930?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Captain Sir Roddy, R.N. (Ret.)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Captain Sir Roddy, R.N. (Ret.)" href="/user/show/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret">Captain Sir Roddy, R.N. (Ret.)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765310101" href="/book/show/8722535-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret?shelf=fantasy-scifi">fantasy-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret?shelf=canadian-authors-translators">canadian-authors-translators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret?shelf=malazan-book-of-the-fallen">malazan-book-of-the-fallen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2482609-captain-sir-roddy-r-n-ret?shelf=author-steven-erikson">author-steven-erikson</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142613930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer591683508149557147">Just like life, all good things must come to an end. I finished reading the tenth, and final, volume in Steven Erikson's amazing series, "A Tale of the Malazan Book of the Fallen." The tenth book is entitled, <i>The Crippled God</i> and is really the second half of the conclusion of the series that was started in the ninth book, <i>Dust of Dreams</i>. If you're going to read <i>The Crippled God</i>, and if it has been some time since you last read <i>Dust of Dreams</i>, I'd strongly urge you to pick it up and re-read it ag</span>
  <span id="freeText591683508149557147" style="display:none">Just like life, all good things must come to an end. I finished reading the tenth, and final, volume in Steven Erikson's amazing series, "A Tale of the Malazan Book of the Fallen." The tenth book is entitled, <i>The Crippled God</i> and is really the second half of the conclusion of the series that was started in the ninth book, <i>Dust of Dreams</i>. If you're going to read <i>The Crippled God</i>, and if it has been some time since you last read <i>Dust of Dreams</i>, I'd strongly urge you to pick it up and re-read it again.<br /><br />I realize that many fans of Erikson's Malazan series have not yet read <i>The Crippled God</i>, or are still working their way through the earlier books in the series for the first time, so I am going to be very, very careful not to spoil one iota of the great adventure that awaits you.<br /><br />It seems pretty obvious to me that only readers of the Malazan series will be reading <i>The Crippled God</i>, and what I can tell you is that you will finish this novel (and the series) and be profoundly satisfied. Let me reiterate--You will be profoundly satisfied! <br /><br />Now, you may hear some reviewers say, "But what about So-and-So, and what about this or that plot thread?" But just like real life, Steven Erikson has concluded the tale with the characters and plot-lines that were required. Think about it like this, not every character that participated in fighting in World War II can appear in every battle during the six years of war. Erikson's "A Tale of the Malazan Book of the Fallen" is just like that too. It is a continuum, a time-line, along which characters and plot-lines appear and come and go. Having said all of this, let me assure you that most of the characters you've come to love and admire (or fear) are all here in <i>The Crippled God</i>.<br /><br />This final book is the poster-child for the definition of an 'epic novel'. It is epic in that it is the final episode in a truly epic series. The series finale contains several amazingly epic plot-lines that reach towering heights in a crescendo of drama, suspense and action; ending with the 'mother of all convergences' that takes up the final one-third of the book. This mythology that is the Malazan world is, in my opinion, only rivaled by that of Homer's tales in <i>The Iliad</i> and <i>The Odyssey</i>. All of the pathos, drama, courage, fears, treachery, visceral horror, and even the acts of human kindness that make up Homer's timeless story of the Trojan War and Odysseus' ten-year journey home to Ithaka, are brilliantly recast for a new age by Steven Erikson in his ten books of "A Tale of the Malazan Book of the Fallen." This is seriously some very good stuff!<br /><br />Maybe it really is best to finish this review by letting Erikson's soldiers of the Malazan Army have the last word--<blockquote>"<i>And now the page before us blurs.<br />An age is done. The book must close.<br />We are abandoned to history.<br />Raise high one more time the tattered standard<br />of the Fallen. See through the drifting smoke<br />to the dark stains upon the fabric.<br />This is the blood of our lives, this is the<br />payment of our deeds, all soon to be<br />forgotten.<br />We were never what people could be.<br />We were only what we were.<br /><br />Remember us</i>."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="591683508149557147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Dara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13656026-dara"><img alt="Dara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500476380p2/13656026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744948064?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10687642-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=lady-protag">lady-protag</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744948064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8667990047134181377"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8447255.The_Crippled_God__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___10_' title='The Crippled God (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #10) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crippled God</a> is the 10th and final book in the Malazan Book of the Fallen series (the main series, anyway). <i>The Crippled God</i> continues the theme of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/938544.Toll_the_Hounds__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___8_' title='Toll the Hounds (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #8) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Toll the Hounds</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4703427.Dust_of_Dreams__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___9_' title='Dust of Dreams (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #9) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dust of Dreams</a>: a lot of internal monologues and philosophizing. I frequently found myself bored. I actually ended up skimming entire sections, which is pretty rare for me. Erikson's writing is still great but it wasn't enough to keep me interested.<br/><br/>The first few chapters are just checking up on various characters. I was keen f</span>
  <span id="freeText8667990047134181377" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8447255.The_Crippled_God__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___10_" title="The Crippled God (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #10) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crippled God</a> is the 10th and final book in the Malazan Book of the Fallen series (the main series, anyway). <i>The Crippled God</i> continues the theme of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/938544.Toll_the_Hounds__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___8_" title="Toll the Hounds (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #8) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Toll the Hounds</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4703427.Dust_of_Dreams__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___9_" title="Dust of Dreams (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #9) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust of Dreams</a>: a lot of internal monologues and philosophizing. I frequently found myself bored. I actually ended up skimming entire sections, which is pretty rare for me. Erikson's writing is still great but it wasn't enough to keep me interested.<br /><br />The first few chapters are just checking up on various characters. I was keen for the story to take off and it took a <i>long</i> time for that to happen. The entire storyline with the Shake felt like filler (more sections that I speed-read) or set-up for the next trilogy of books. I also had some issues with some narrative choices. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[First, the Forkrul Assail were suddenly the Big Bad? There were always whispers about them but their desire to rid the world of humans seemed to come out of nowhere. I also was kind of jarred by the decision to make the Crippled God himself a sympathetic character. He was built up to be this big, evil force and suddenly we are supposed to feel bad for him? Wasn't my favorite development. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All that out of the way, the final few chapters were great. I liked how things came together while leaving some things mysterious. Erikson wove things together really well but it also felt kind of abrupt. I would have liked to spent more time with some old favorites like Karsa, Kruppe, Tehol, and Bugg but maybe they'll have stories in another book.<br /><br />This definitely isn't my favorite entry in the series but it offers a satisfying conclusion to the story. 10,000+ pages, 10 books, and over a year of reading but I'm glad that I went on this journey with these characters. I'm gonna miss them.<br /><br /><b>C+</b><br /><br />Series rating: <b>A</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8667990047134181377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8520844988283175510">5 stars isn't enough for this book and this series as a whole. Breaking down something this vast and amazing into a star rating just seems wrong somehow. I don't know if I'll ever experience something like this again. <br/><br/>The Book of the Fallen is now what I will compare all other epic fantasy books to, that is the watermark. While I'm glad I made it through, I'm just as sad that it's over. I can't believe how powerful this series was and how it made me feel along the way. So many heart breaks, but </span>
  <span id="freeText8520844988283175510" style="display:none">5 stars isn't enough for this book and this series as a whole. Breaking down something this vast and amazing into a star rating just seems wrong somehow. I don't know if I'll ever experience something like this again. <br /><br />The Book of the Fallen is now what I will compare all other epic fantasy books to, that is the watermark. While I'm glad I made it through, I'm just as sad that it's over. I can't believe how powerful this series was and how it made me feel along the way. So many heart breaks, but also just as many laughs and moments of sheer joy. This was great, that's all I can say. I'll never forgot my year of the fallen. <br /><br />"And only the fallen can rise again."</span>

<div id="review_522878602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/522878602" />
    <a title="Artemas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6751111-artemas"><img alt="Artemas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452871375p2/6751111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/522878602?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Artemas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Artemas" href="/user/show/6751111-artemas">Artemas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553813180" href="/book/show/11701178-the-crippled-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=military-fiction">military-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=gritty-fantasy">gritty-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=1000-pages-plus">1000-pages-plus</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer522878602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2507507652015028175">As a whole I loved the Malazan Book of the Fallen series. However, <i>the Crippled God</i> really left me with some serious questions as to why Erikson ended this epic series the way he did. For me it felt like the author originally wanted to have 11 books in the series and the publishers made him drop it down to 10 at the last second.<br/><br/>I am not going to give away anything specific, but there were some major characters who did not come remotely close to having the impact in the end that I believed the se</span>
  <span id="freeText2507507652015028175" style="display:none">As a whole I loved the Malazan Book of the Fallen series. However, <i>the Crippled God</i> really left me with some serious questions as to why Erikson ended this epic series the way he did. For me it felt like the author originally wanted to have 11 books in the series and the publishers made him drop it down to 10 at the last second.<br /><br />I am not going to give away anything specific, but there were some major characters who did not come remotely close to having the impact in the end that I believed the series was building toward. Other key events were just skipped over while there were many scenes that I felt dragged on for far too long.<br /><br />Malazan Book of the Fallen, 10 Book Series = 5 stars<br />The Crippled God = 3 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="2507507652015028175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BIL93yAnGkgb+Z9qgxLJUexH4B360tElWh9J2sb21UqGRlxwa7mWHLMEVjS/D4H7OiDl+3Ut03djzX4iACTrTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+SPOiRSiBQMHlO8qLI87Mm+45heYWoGD6ZJRjb/NGYt7528mXzyJV69pJnQQknOYud/j8Relg9HQQGZ1eR8njw==')})
  }
//]]>
